Metadata is sent in batches, but is not parallelized.\n551: // This is only used for the metadata_config.send setting and 1.x Remote Write.\n552: func (t *QueueManager) AppendWatcherMetadata(ctx context.Context, metadata []scrape.MetricMetadata) {\n553: \t// no op for any newer proto format, which will cache metadata sent to it from the WAL watcher.\n554: \tif t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n555: \t\treturn\n556: \t}\n557: \n558: \t// 1.X will still get metadata in batches.\n559: \tmm := make([]prompb.MetricMetadata, 0, len(metadata))\n560: \tfor _, entry := range metadata {\n561: \t\tmm = append(mm, prompb.MetricMetadata{\n562: \t\t\tMetricFamilyName: entry.MetricFamily,\n563: \t\t\tHelp:             entry.Help,\n564: \t\t\tType:             prompb.FromMetadataType(entry.Type),\n565: \t\t\tUnit:             entry.Unit,\n566: \t\t})\n567: \t}\n568: \n569: \tpBuf := proto.NewBuffer(nil)\n570: \tnumSends := int(math.Ceil(float64(len(metadata)) / float64(t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend)))\n571: \tfor i := range numSends {\n572: \t\tlast := min((i+1)*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, len(metadata))\n573: \t\terr := \t\t\tt.logger.Error(\"non-recoverable error while sending metadata\", \"count\", last-(i*t.mcfg.MaxSamplesPerSend), \"err\", err)\n577: \t\t}\n578: \t}\n579: }\n580: \n581: func (t *QueueManager) sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, metadata []prompb.MetricMetadata, pBuf *proto.Buffer) error {\n582: \t// Build the WriteRequest with no samples (v1 flow).\n583: \treq, _, _, err := buildWriteRequest(t.logger, nil, metadata, pBuf, nil, nil, t.compr)\n584: \tif err != nil {\n585: \t\treturn err\n586: \t}\n587: \n588: \tmetadataCount := len(metadata)\n589: \n590: \tattemptStore := func(try int) error {\n591: \t\tctx, span := otel.Tracer(\"\").Start(ctx, \"Remote Metadata Send Batch\")\n592: \t\tdefer span.End()\n593: \n594: \t\tspan.SetAttributes(\n595: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"metadata\", metadataCount),\n596: \t\t\tattribute.Int(\"try\", try),\n597: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_name\", t.storeClient.Name()),\n598: \t\t\tattribute.String(\"remote_url\", t.storeClient.Endpoint()),\n599: \t\t)\n600: \t\t// Attributes defined by OpenTelemetry semantic conventions.\n601: \t\tif try > 0 {\n602: \t\t\tspan.SetAttributes(semconv.HTTPResendCount(try))\n603: \t\t}\n604: \n605: \t\tbegin := time.Now()\n606: \t\t// Ignoring WriteResponseStats, because there is nothing for metadata, since it's\n607: \t\t// embedded in v2 calls now, and we do v1 here.\n608: \t\t_, err := t.storeClient.Store(ctx, req, try)\n609: \t\tt.metrics.sentBatchDuration.Observe(time.Since(begin).Seconds())\n610: \n611: \t\tif err != nil {\n612: \t\t\tspan.RecordError(err)\n613: \t\t\treturn err\n614: \t\t}\n615: \t\treturn nil\n616: \t}\n617: \n618: \tretry := func() {\n619: \t\tt.metrics.retriedMetadataTotal.Add(float64(len(metadata)))\n620: \t}\n621: \terr = t.sendWriteRequestWithBackoff(ctx, attemptStore, retry)\n622: \tif err != nil {\n623: \t\treturn err\n624: \t}\n625: \tt.metrics.metadataTotal.Add(float64(len(metadata)))\n626: \tt.metrics.metadataBytesTotal.Add(float64(len(req)))\n627: \treturn nil\n628: }\n629: \n630: func isSampleOld(baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration, ts int64) bool {\n631: \tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n632: \t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n633: \t\treturn false\n634: \t}\n635: \tlimitTs := baseTime.Add(-sampleAgeLimit)\n636: \tsampleTs := timestamp.Time(ts)\n637: \treturn sampleTs.Before(limitTs)\n638: }\n639: \n640: func isTimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n641: \treturn func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n642: \t\tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n643: \t\t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n644: \t\t\treturn false\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tswitch {\n647: \t\t// Only the first element should be set in the series, therefore we only check the first element.\n648: \t\tcase len(ts.Samples) > 0:\n649: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, sampleAgeLimit, ts.Samples[0].Timestamp) {\n650: \t\t\t\tmetrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n651: \t\t\t\treturn true\n652: \t\t\t}\n653: \t\tcase len(ts.Histograms) > 0:\n654: \t\t\tif isSampleOld(baseTime, \t\t\t}\n663: \t\tdefault:\n664: \t\t\treturn false\n665: \t\t}\n666: \t\treturn false\n667: \t}\n668: }\n669: \n670: func isV2TimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n671: \treturn func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n672: \t\tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n673: \t\t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we Blocks until all samples are\n701: // enqueued on their shards or a shutdown signal is received.\n702: func (t *QueueManager) Append(samples []record.RefSample) bool {\n703: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n704: outer:\n705: \tfor _, s := range samples {\n706: \t\tif isSampleOld(currentTime, time.Duration(t.cfg.SampleAgeLimit), s.T) {\n707: \t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n708: \t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t}\n710: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n711: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[s.Ref]\n712: \t\tif !ok {\n713: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[s.Ref]; !ok {\n714: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Dropped sample for series that was not explicitly dropped via relabelling\", \"ref\", s.Ref)\n715: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n716: \t\t\t} else {\n717: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n718: \t\t\t}\n719: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n720: \t\t\tcontinue\n721: \t\t}\n722: \t\t// TODO(cstyan): Handle or at least log an error if no metadata is found.\n723: \t\t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n724: \t\tmeta := t.seriesMetadata[s.Ref]\n725: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n726: \t\t// Start with a very small backoff. This should not be t.cfg.MinBackoff\n727: \t\t// as it can happen without errors, and we want to pickup work after\n728: \t\t// filling a queue/resharding as quickly as possible.\n729: \t\t// TODO: Consider using the average duration of a request as the backoff.\n730: \t\tbackoff := model.Duration(5 * time.Millisecond)\n731: \t\tfor {\n732: \t\t\tselect {\n733: \t\t\tcase <-t.quit:\n734: \t\t\t\treturn false\n735: \t\t\tdefault:\n736: \t\t\t}\n737: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(s.Ref, timeSeries{\n738: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels: lbls,\n739: \t\t\t\tmetadata:     meta,\n740: \t\t\t\ttimestamp:    s.T,\n741: \t\t\t\tvalue:        s.V,\n742: \t\t\t\tsType:        tSample,\n743: \t\t\t}) {\n744: \t\t\t\tcontinue outer\n745: \t\t\t}\n746: \n747: \t\t\tt.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n748: \t\t\ttime.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n749: \t\t\tbackoff *= 2\n750: \t\t\t// It is reasonable to use t.cfg.MaxBackoff here, as if we have hit\n751: \t\t\t// the full backoff we are likely waiting for external resources.\n752: \t\t\tif backoff > t.cfg.MaxBackoff {\n753: \t\t\t\tbackoff = t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n754: \t\t\t}\n755: \t\t}\n756: \t}\n757: \treturn true\n758: }\n759: \n760: func (t *QueueManager) AppendExemplars(exemplars []record.RefExemplar) bool {\n761: \tif !t.sendExemplars {\n762: \t\treturn true\n763: \t}\n764: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n765: outer:\n766: \tfor _, e := \t\t\tcontinue\n770: \t\t}\n771: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n772: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[e.Ref]\n773: \t\tif !ok {\n774: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[e.Ref]; !ok {\n775: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n777: \t\t\t} else {\n778: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n779: \t\t\t}\n780: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n781: \t\t\tcontinue\n782: \t\t}\n783: \t\tmeta := {\n789: \t\t\tcase <-t.quit:\n790: \t\t\t\treturn false\n791: \t\t\tdefault:\n792: \t\t\t}\n793: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(e.Ref, timeSeries{\n794: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels:   lbls,\n795: \t\t\t\tmetadata:       meta,\n796: \t\t\t\ttimestamp:      e.T,\n797: \t\t\t\tvalue:          e.V,\n798: \t\t\t\texemplarLabels: e.Labels,\n799: \t\t\t\tsType:          tExemplar,\n800: \t\t\t}) {\n801: \t\t\t\tcontinue outer\n802: \t\t\t}\n803: \n804: \t\t\tt.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n805: \t\t\ttime.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n806: \t\t\tbackoff *= 2\n807: \t\t\tif backoff > t.cfg.MaxBackoff {\n808: \t\t\t\tbackoff = t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n809: \t\t\t}\n810: \t\t}\n811: \t}\n812: \treturn true\n813: }\n814: \n815: func (t *QueueManager) AppendHistograms(histograms \treturn true\n867: }\n868: \n869: func (t *QueueManager) AppendFloatHistograms(floatHistograms []record.RefFloatHistogramSample) bool {\n870: \tif !t.sendNativeHistograms {\n871: \t\treturn true\n872: \t}\n873: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n874: outer:\n875: \tfor _, h := range floatHistograms {\n876: \t\tif isSampleOld(currentTime, time.Duration(t.cfg.SampleAgeLimit), h.T) {\n877: \t\t\tt.metrics.droppedHistogramsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n878: \t\t\tcontinue\n879: \t\t}\n880: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n881: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[h.Ref]\n882: \t\tif !ok {\n883: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[h.Ref]; !ok {\n884: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Dropped histogram for series that was not explicitly dropped via relabelling\", \"ref\", h.Ref)\n885: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedHistogramsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n886: \t\t\t} else {\n887: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedHistogramsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n888: \t\t\t}\n889: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n890: \t\t\tcontinue\n891: \t\t}\n892: \t\tmeta := \t\t\t\treturn false\n900: \t\t\tdefault:\n901: \t\t\t}\n902: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(h.Ref, timeSeries{\n903: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels:   lbls,\n904: \t\t\t\tmetadata:       meta,\n905: \t\t\t\ttimestamp:      h.T,\n906: \t\t\t\tfloatHistogram: h.FH,\n907: \t\t\t\tsType:          tFloatHistogram,\n908: \t\t\t}) {\n909: \t\t\t\tcontinue outer\n910: \t\t\t}\n911: \n912: t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n917: \t\t\t}\n918: \t\t}\n919: \t}\n920: \treturn true\n921: }\n922: \n923: // Start the queue manager sending samples to the remote storage.\n924: // Does not block.\n925: func (t *QueueManager) Start() {\n926: \t// Register and initialise some metrics.\n927: \tt.metrics.register()\n928: \tt.metrics.shardCapacity.Set(float64(t.cfg.Capacity))\n929: \tt.metrics.maxNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MaxShards))\n930: \tt.metrics.minNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n931: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n932: \tt.metrics.maxSamplesPerSend.Set(float64(t.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend))\n933: \n934: \tt.shards.start(t.numShards)\n935: \tt.watcher.Start()\n936: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n937: and waits for pending\n946: // sends to complete.\n947: func (t *QueueManager) Stop() {\n948: \tt.logger.Info(\"Stopping remote storage...\")\n949: \tdefer t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage stopped.\")\n950: \n951: \tclose(t.quit)\n952: \tt.wg.Wait()\n953: \t// Wait for all QueueManager routines to end before stopping shards, metadata watcher, and WAL watcher. This\n954: \t// is to ensure we don't end up executing a reshard and shards.stop() at the same time, which\n955: \t// causes a closed channel panic.\n956: \tt.shards.stop()\n957: \tt.watcher.Stop()\n958: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n959: \t\tt.metadataWatcher.Stop()\n960: \t}\n961: \tt.metrics.unregister()\n962: }\n963: \n964: // StoreSeries keeps track of which series we know about for lookups when sending samples to remote.\n965: func (t *QueueManager) StoreSeries(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n966: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n967: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n968: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n969: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n970: \tfor _, s := range series {\n971: \t\t// Just make sure all the Refs of Series will insert into seriesSegmentIndexes map StoreMetadata(meta []record.RefMetadata) {\n988: \tif t.protoMsg == config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n989: \t\treturn\n990: \t}\n991: \n992: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n993: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n994: \t}\n1001: }\n1002: \n1003: // UpdateSeriesSegment updates the segment number held against the series,\n1004: // so we can trim older ones in SeriesReset.\n1005: func (t *QueueManager) UpdateSeriesSegment(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n1006: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1007: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1008: \tfor _, s := range series {\n1009: \t\tt.seriesSegmentIndexes[s.Ref] = index\n1010: \t}\n1011: }\n1012: \n1013: // SeriesReset is used when reading a checkpoint. WAL Watcher should have\n1014: // stored series records with the checkpoints index number, so we can now\n1015: // delete any ref ID's lower than that # from the two maps.\n1016: func (t *QueueManager) SeriesReset(index int) {\n1017: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n1018: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n1019: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1020: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1021: \t// Check for series that are in segments older than the checkpoint\n1022: \t// that were not also present in the checkpoint.\n1023: \tfor k, v := range t.seriesSegmentIndexes {\n1024: \t\tif v < index {\n1025: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesSegmentIndexes, k)\n1026: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesLabels, k)\n1027: \t\t\tdelete(t.seriesMetadata, k)\n1028: \t\t\tdelete(t.droppedSeries, k)\n1029: \t\t}\n1030: \t}\n1031: }\n1032: \n1033: // SetClient updates the client used by a queue. Used when only client specific\n1034: // fields are updated to avoid restarting the queue.\n1035: func (t *QueueManager) SetClient(c WriteClient) {\n1036: \tt.clientMtx.Lock()\n1037: \tt.storeClient = c\n1038: \tt.clientMtx.Unlock()\n1039: }\n1040: \n1041: func (t *QueueManager) client() WriteClient {\n1042: \tt.clientMtx.RLock()\n1043: \tdefer t.clientMtx.RUnlock()\n1044: \treturn t.storeClient\n1045: }\n1046: \n1047: // processExternalLabels merges externalLabels into b. If b contains\n1048: // a label in externalLabels, the value in b wins.\n1049: func processExternalLabels(b *labels.Builder, externalLabels []labels.Label) {\n1050: \tfor _, el := range externalLabels {\n1051: \t\tif b.Get(el.Name) == \"\" {\n1052: \t\t\tb.Set(el.Name, el.Value)\n1053: \t\t}\n1054: \t}\n1055: }\n1056: \n1057: func (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n1058: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1059: \n1060: \tticker := time.NewTicker(shardUpdateDuration)\n1061: \tdefer ticker.Stop()\n1062: \tfor {\n1063: \t\tselect {\n1064: \t\tcase <-ticker.C:\n1065: \t\t\tdesiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()\n1066: \t\t\tif !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {\n1067: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1068: \t\t\t}\n1069: \t\t\t// Resharding can take some time, and we want this loop\n1070: \t\t\t// to stay close to shardUpdateDuration.\n1071: \t\t\tselect {\n1072: \t\t\tcase t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n1073: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n1074: \t\t\t\tt.numShards = desiredShards\n1075: \t\t\tdefault:\n1076: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Currently resharding, skipping.\")\n1077: \t\t\t}\n1078: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1079: \t\t\treturn\n1080: \t\t}\n1081: \t}\n1082: }\n1083: \n1084: // shouldReshard returns whether resharding should occur.\n1085: func (t *QueueManager) shouldReshard(desiredShards int) bool {\n1086: \tif desiredShards == t.numShards {\n1087: \t\treturn false\n1088: \t}\n1089: \t// We shouldn't reshard if Prometheus hasn't been able to send\n1090: \t// since the last time it checked if it should reshard.\n1091: \tminSendTimestamp := time.Now().Add(-1 * shardUpdateDuration).Unix()\n1092: \tlsts := t.lastSendTimestamp.Load()\n1093: \tif lsts < minSendTimestamp {\n1094: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold\", \"lastSendTimestamp\", lsts, \"minSendTimestamp\", minSendTimestamp)\n1095: \t\treturn false\n1096: \t}\n1097: \tif disableTimestamp := t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp.Load(); time.Now().Unix() < disableTimestamp {\n1098: \t\tdisabledAt := time.Unix(t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Load(), 0)\n1099: \t\tdisabledFor := time.Until(time.Unix(disableTimestamp, 0))\n1100: \n1101: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled while waiting for recoverable errors\", \"disabled_at\", disabledAt, \"disabled_for\", disabledFor)\n1102: \t\treturn false\n1103: \t}\n1104: \treturn true\n1105: }\n1106: \n1107: // calculateDesiredShards returns the number of desired shards, which will be\n1108: // the current QueueManager.numShards if resharding should not occur for reasons\n1109: // outlined in this functions implementation. It is up to the caller to reshard, or not,\n1110: // based on the return value.\n1111: func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {\n1112: \tt.dataIn.tick()\n1113: \tt.dataOut.tick()\n1114: \tt.dataOutDuration.tick()\n1115: \n1116: \t// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we\n1117: \t// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples\n1118: \t// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average\n1119: \t// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.\n1120: \tvar (\n1121: \t\tdataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()\n1122: \t\tdataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()\n1123: \t\tdataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)\n1124: \t\tdataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate\n1125: \t\thighestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()\n1126: \t\thighestRecv     = t.metrics.highestTimestamp.Get()\n1127: \t\tdelay           = highestRecv - highestSent\n1128: \t\tdataPending     = delay * dataInRate\n1129: \t)\n1130: \n1131: \tif dataOutRate <= 0 {\n1132: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1133: \t}\n1134: \n1135: \tvar (\n1136: \t\t// When behind we will try to catch up on 5% of samples per second.\n1137: \t\tbacklogCatchup = 0.05 * dataPending\n1138: \t\t// Calculate Time to send one sample, averaged across all sends done this tick.\n1139: \t\ttimePerSample = dataOutDuration / dataOutRate\n1140: \t\tdesiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)\n1141: \t)\n1142: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(desiredShards)\n1143: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\",\n1144: \t\t\"dataInRate\", dataInRate,\n1145: \t\t\"dataOutRate\", dataOutRate,\n1146: \t\t\"dataPendingRate\", dataPendingRate,\n1147: \t\t\"dataPending\", dataPending,\n1148: \t\t\"dataOutDuration\", dataOutDuration,\n1149: \t\t\"timePerSample\", timePerSample,\n1150: \t\t\"desiredShards\", desiredShards,\n1151: \t\t\"highestSent\", highestSent,\n1152: \t\t\"highestRecv\", highestRecv,\n1153: \t)\n1154: \n1155: \t// Changes in the number of shards must be greater than shardToleranceFraction.\n1156: \tvar (\n1157: \t\tlowerBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. - shardToleranceFraction)\n1158: \t\tupperBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. + shardToleranceFraction)\n1159: \t)\n1160: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.updateShardsLoop\",\n1161: \t\t\"lowerBound\", lowerBound, \"desiredShards\", desiredShards, \"upperBound\", upperBound)\n1162: \n1163: \tdesiredShards = math.Ceil(desiredShards) // Round up to be on the safe side.\n1164: \tif lowerBound <= desiredShards && desiredShards <= upperBound {\n1165: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1166: \t}\n1167: \n1168: \tnumShards := int(desiredShards)\n1169: \t// Do not downshard if we are more than ten seconds back.\n1170: \tif numShards < t.numShards && delay > 10.0 {\n1171: \t\tt.logger.Debug(\"Not downsharding due to being too far behind\")\n1172: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1173: \t}\n1174: \n1175: \tswitch {\n1176: \tcase numShards > t.cfg.MaxShards:\n1177: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MaxShards\n1178: \tcase numShards < t.cfg.MinShards:\n1179: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MinShards\n1180: \t}\n1181: \treturn numShards\n1182: }\n1183: \n1184: func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n1185: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1186: \n1187: \tfor {\n1188: \t\tselect {\n1189: \t\tcase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n1190: \t\t\t// We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n1191: \t\t\t// flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n1192: \t\t\t// order.\n1193: \t\t\tt.shards.stop()\n1194: \t\t\tt.shards.start(numShards)\n1195: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1196: \t\t\treturn\n1197: \t\t}\n1198: \t}\n1199: }\n1200: \n1201: func (t *QueueManager) newShards() *shards {\n1202: \ts := &shards{\n1203: \t\tqm:   t,\n1204: \t\tdone: make(chan struct{}),\n1205: \t}\n1206: \treturn s\n1207: }\n1208: \n1209: type shards struct {\n1210: \tmtx sync.RWMutex // With the WAL, this is never actually contended.\n1211: \n1212: \tqm     *QueueManager\n1213: \tqueues []*queue\n1214: \t// So we can accurately track how many of each are lost during shard shutdowns.\n1215: \tenqueuedSamples    atomic.Int64\n1216: \tenqueuedExemplars  atomic.Int64\n1217: \tenqueuedHistograms atomic.Int64\n1218: \n1219: \t// Emulate a wait group with a channel and an atomic int, as you\n1220: \t// cannot select on a wait group.\n1221: \tdone    chan struct{}\n1222: \trunning atomic.Int32\n1223: \n1224: \t// Soft shutdown context will prevent new enqueues and deadlocks.\n1225: \tsoftShutdown chan struct{}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Hard shutdown context is used to terminate outgoing HTTP connections\n1228: \t// after giving them a chance to terminate.\n1229: \thardShutdown                    context.CancelFunc\n1230: \tsamplesDroppedOnHardShutdown    atomic.Uint32\n1231: \texemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown  atomic.Uint32\n1232: \thistogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown atomic.Uint32\n1233: \tmetadataDroppedOnHardShutdown   atomic.Uint32\n1234: }\n1235: \n1236: // start the shards; must be called before any call to enqueue.\n1237: func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n1238: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1239: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1240: \n1241: \ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n1242: \ts.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n1243: \n1244: \tnewQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n1245: \tfor i := range n {\n1246: \t\tnewQueues[i] = newQueue(s.qm.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, s.qm.cfg.Capacity)\n1247: \t}\n1248: \n1249: \ts.queues = newQueues\n1250: \n1251: \tvar hardShutdownCtx context.Context\n1252: \thardShutdownCtx, s.hardShutdown = context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n1253: \ts.softShutdown = make(chan struct{})\n1254: \ts.running.Store(int32(n))\n1255: \ts.done = make(chan struct{})\n1256: \ts.enqueuedSamples.Store(0)\n1257: \ts.enqueuedExemplars.Store(0)\n1258: \ts.enqueuedHistograms.Store(0)\n1259: \ts.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1260: \ts.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1261: \ts.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1262: \ts.metadataDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1263: \tfor i := range n {\n1264: \t\tgo s.runShard(hardShutdownCtx, i, newQueues[i])\n1265: \t}\n1266: }\n1267: \n1268: // stop the shards; subsequent call to enqueue will return false.\n1269: func (s *shards) stop() {\n1270: \t// Attempt a clean shutdown, but only wait flushDeadline for all the shards\n1271: \t// to cleanly exit. As we're doing RPCs, enqueue can block indefinitely.\n1272: \t// We must be able so call stop concurrently, hence we can only take the\n1273: \t// RLock here.\n1274: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1275: \tclose(s.softShutdown)\n1276: \ts.mtx.RUnlock()\n1277: \n1278: \t// Enqueue should now be unblocked, so we can take the write lock.  This\n1279: \t// also ensures we don't race with writes to the queues, and get a panic:\n1280: \t// send on closed channel.\n1281: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1282: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1283: \tfor _, queue := range s.queues {\n1284: \t\tgo queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n1285: \t}\n1286: \tselect {\n1287: \tcase <-s.done:\n1288: \t\treturn\n1289: \tcase <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n1290: \t}\n1291: \n1292: \t// Force an unclean shutdown.\n1293: \ts.hardShutdown()\n1294: \t<-s.done\n1295: \n1296: \t// Log error for any dropped samples, exemplars, or histograms.\n1297: \tlogDroppedError := func(t string, counter atomic.Uint32) {\n1298: \t\tif dropped := counter.Load(); dropped > 0 {\n1299: \t\t\ts.qm.logger.Error(fmt.Sprintf(\"Failed to flush all %s on shutdown\", t), \"count\", dropped)\n1300: \t\t}\n1301: \t}\n1302: \tlogDroppedError(\"samples\", s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1303: \tlogDroppedError(\"exemplars\", s.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1304: \tlogDroppedError(\"histograms\", s.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1305: }\n1306: \n1307: // enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or\n1308: // resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and\n1309: // retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,\n1310: // specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the\n1311: // partial batch has also been filled.\n1312: func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n1313: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1314: \tdefer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n1315: \tshard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n1316: \tselect {\n1317: \tcase <-s.softShutdown:\n1318: \t\treturn false\n1319: \tdefault:\n1320: \t\tappended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n1321: \t\tif !appended {\n1322: \t\t\treturn false\n1323: \t\t}\n1324: \t\tswitch data.sType {\n1325: \t\tcase tSample:\n1326: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n1327: \t\t\ts.enqueuedSamples.Inc()\n1328: \t\tcase tExemplar:\n1329: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Inc()\n1330: \t\t\ts.enqueuedExemplars.Inc()\n1331: \t\tcase tHistogram, tFloatHistogram:\n1332: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Inc()\n1333: \t\t\ts.enqueuedHistograms.Inc()\n1334: \t\tdefault:\n1335: \t\t\treturn true\n1336: \t\t}\n1337: \t\ts.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set(float64(data.timestamp / 1000))\n1338: \t\ts.qm.dataIn.incr(1)\n1339: \t\treturn true\n1340: \t}\n1341: }\n1342: \n1343: type queue struct {\n1344: \t// batchMtx covers operations appending to or publishing the partial batch.\n1345: \tbatchMtx   sync.Mutex\n1346: \tbatch      []timeSeries\n1347: \tbatchQueue chan []timeSeries\n1348: \n1349: \t// Since we know there are a limited number of batches out, using a stack\n1350: \t// is easy and safe so a sync.Pool is not necessary.\n1351: \t// poolMtx covers adding and removing batches from the batchPool.\n1352: \tpoolMtx   sync.Mutex\n1353: \tbatchPool [][]timeSeries\n1354: }\n1355: \n1356: type timeSeries struct {\n1357: \tseriesLabels   labels.Labels\n1358: \tvalue          float64\n1359: \thistogram      *histogram.Histogram\n1360: \tfloatHistogram *histogram.FloatHistogram\n1361: \tmetadata       *metadata.Metadata\n1362: \ttimestamp      int64\n1363: \texemplarLabels labels.Labels\n1364: \t// The type of series: sample, exemplar, or histogram.\n1365: \tsType seriesType\n1366: }\n1367: \n1368: type seriesType int\n1369: \n1370: const (\n1371: \ttSample seriesType = iota\n1372: \ttExemplar\n1373: \ttHistogram\n1374: \ttFloatHistogram\n1375: \ttMetadata\n1376: )\n1377: \n1378: func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {\n1379: \tbatches := capacity / batchSize\n1380: \t// Always create an unbuffered channel even if capacity is configured to be\n1381: \t// less than max_samples_per_send.\n1382: \tif batches == 0 {\n1383: \t\tbatches = 1\n1384: \t}\n1385: \treturn &queue{\n1386: \t\tbatch:      make([]timeSeries, 0, batchSize),\n1387: \t\tbatchQueue: make(chan []timeSeries, batches),\n1388: \t\t// batchPool should have capacity for everything in the channel + 1 for\n1389: \t\t// the batch being processed.\n1390: \t\tbatchPool: make([][]timeSeries, 0, batches+1),\n1391: \t}\n1392: }\n1393: \n1394: // Append the timeSeries to the buffered batch. Returns false if it\n1395: // cannot be added and must be retried.\n1396: func (q *queue) Append(datum timeSeries) bool {\n1397: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1398: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1399: \t// TODO(cstyan): Check if metadata now means we've reduced the total # of samples\n1400: \t// we can batch together here, and if so find a way to not include metadata\n1401: \t// in the batch size calculation.\n1402: \t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n1403: \tq.batch = append(q.batch, datum)\n1404: \tif len(q.batch) == cap(q.batch) {\n1405: \t\tselect {\n1406: \t\tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1407: \t\t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(q.batch))\n1408: \t\t\treturn true\n1409: \t\tdefault:\n1410: \t\t\t// Remove the sample we just appended. It will get retried.\n1411: \t\t\tq.batch = q.batch[:len(q.batch)-1]\n1412: \t\t\treturn false\n1413: \t\t}\n1414: \t}\n1415: \treturn true\n1416: }\n1417: \n1418: func (q *queue) Chan() <-chan []timeSeries {\n1419: \treturn q.batchQueue\n1420: }\n1421: \n1422: // Batch returns the current batch and allocates a new batch.\n1423: func (q *queue) Batch() []timeSeries {\n1424: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1425: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1426: \tselect {\n1427: \tcase batch := <-q.batchQueue:\n1428: \t\treturn batch\n1429: \tdefault:\n1430: \t\tbatch := q.batch\n1431: \t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(batch))\n1432: \t\treturn batch\n1433: \t}\n1434: }\n1435: \n1436: // ReturnForReuse adds the batch buffer back to the internal pool.\n1437: func (q *queue) ReturnForReuse(batch []timeSeries) {\n1438: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1439: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1440: \tif len(q.batchPool) < cap(q.batchPool) {\n1441: \t\tq.batchPool = append(q.batchPool, batch[:0])\n1442: \t}\n1443: }\n1444: \n1445: // FlushAndShutdown stops the queue and flushes any samples. No appends can be\n1446: // made after this is called.\n1447: func (q *queue) FlushAndShutdown(done <-chan struct{}) {\n1448: \tfor q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {\n1449: \t\ttime.Sleep(time.Second)\n1450: \t}\n1451: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1452: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1453: \tq.batch = nil\n1454: \tclose(q.batchQueue)\n1455: }\n1456: \n1457: // tryEnqueueingBatch tries to send a batch if necessary. If sending needs to\n1458: // be retried it will return true.\n1459: func (q *queue) tryEnqueueingBatch(done <-chan struct{}) bool {\n1460: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1461: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1462: \tif len(q.batch) == 0 {\n1463: \t\treturn false\n1464: \t}\n1465: \n1466: \tselect {\n1467: \tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1468: \t\treturn false\n1469: \tcase <-done:\n1470: \t\t// The shard has been hard shut down, so no more samples can be sent.\n1471: \t\t// No need to try again as we will drop everything left in the queue.\n1472: \t\treturn false\n1473: \tdefault:\n1474: \t\t// The batchQueue is full, so we need to try again later.\n1475: \t\treturn true\n1476: \t}\n1477: }\n1478: \n1479: func (q *queue) newBatch(capacity int) []timeSeries {\n1480: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1481: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1482: \tbatches := len(q.batchPool)\n1483: \tif batches > 0 {\n1484: \t\tbatch := q.batchPool[batches-1]\n1485: \t\tq.batchPool = q.batchPool[:batches-1]\n1486: \t\treturn batch\n1487: \t}\n1488: \treturn make([]timeSeries, 0, capacity)\n1489: }\n1490: \n1491: func (s *shards) runShard(ctx context.Context, shardID int, queue *queue) {\n1492: \tdefer func() {\n1493: \t\tif s.running.Dec() == 0 {\n1494: \t\t\tclose(s.done)\n1495: \t\t}\n1496: \t}()\n1497: \n1498: \tshardNum := strconv.Itoa(shardID)\n1499: \tsymbolTable := \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Sub(float64(droppedHistograms))\n1572: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n1573: \n1604: func populateTimeSeries(batch []timeSeries, pendingData []prompb.TimeSeries, sendExemplars, sendNativeHistograms bool) (int, int, int) {\n1605: \tvar nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, sendSamplesWithBackoff to the remote storage with backoff for recoverable errors.\n1698: func (s *shards) sendSamplesWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, samples []prompb.TimeSeries, sampleCount, The key problem I see is in the resharding mechanism. Let me trace through:\n\n1. In updateShardsLoop (line 1057-1082), when a reshard is needed:\n   - It calculates desired shards\n   - It sends to reshardChan (line 1072)\n   - It updates `t.numShards` (line 1074) to the desired shard count\n\n2. In reshardLoop (line 1184-1199):\n   - Receives the desired number of shards from reshardChan\n   - Calls `t.shards.stop()` (line 1193) - stops old shards\n   - Calls `t.shards.start(numShards)` (line 1194) - starts new shards with new shard count\n\n3. In enqueue (line 1312-1341):\n   - Computes `shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))` (line 1315)\n   - This uses the current queue count to determine which queue to write to\n\nNow here's the race condition:\n\nIf updateShardsLoop is executing and:\n1. It calls `t.shards.stop()` at time T1 (which closes softShutdown and causes enqueue to fail)\n2. But before it calls `t.shards.start(newShards)` at T2\n3. New Append() calls come in from the WAL watcher\n4. These calls get rejected because `s.softShutdown` is closed (line 1317-1318)\n\nActually, let me re-read more carefully. Looking at line 1072-1074:\n```go\ncase t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n    t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n    t.numShards = desiredShards\n\n\n```\n\nThis is in updateShardsLoop, and it updates `t.numShards` immediately. However, the value being sent on reshardChan is the OLD numShards value. Let me trace the actual issue more carefully.\n\nLooking at reshardLoop, when it receives numShards from the channel, it stops the old shards completely to ensure all samples are flushed before starting new ones. The design intent is to guarantee samples are delivered in order by fully draining old shards before initializing replacements.\n\nIn the enqueue function, samples route to shards using `shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))`. The problem emerges during resharding: when reshardLoop calls `t.shards.stop()`, it closes the softShutdown channel, causing all subsequent enqueue calls to fail until `t.shards.start(numShards)` completes. Samples being enqueued concurrently during this transition window can be lost or misrouted.\n\n```\n\ngo\nfunc (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n    s.mtx.RLock()\n    defer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n    shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n    select {\n    case <-s.softShutdown:\n        return false\n    default:\n        appended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n        ...\n    }\n}\n```\n\nWhen softShutdown closes, the select immediately returns false. The testReshardPartialBatch test (lines 592-633) appears designed to verify the system handles deadlocks correctly when resharding occurs with concurrent enqueue endpoint. #15399\\n191: \\n192: ## 3.0.0 / 2024-11-14\\n193: \\n194: This release includes new features such as a brand new UI and UTF-8 support enabled by default. As this marks the first new major version in seven years, several breaking changes are introduced. The breaking changes are mainly around the removal of deprecated feature flags and CLI arguments, and the full list can be found below. For users that want to upgrade we recommend to read through our [migration guide](https://prometheus.io/docs/prometheus/3.0/migration/).\\n195: \\n196: * [CHANGE] Set the `GOMAXPROCS` variable automatically to match the Linux CPU quota. Use `--no-auto-gomaxprocs` to disable it. The `auto-gomaxprocs` feature flag was removed. #15376\\n197: * [CHANGE] Set the `GOMEMLIMIT` variable automatically to match the Linux container memory limit. Use `--no-auto-gomemlimit` to disable it. The `auto-gomemlimit` feature flag was removed. #15373\\n198: * [CHANGE] Scraping: Remove implicit fallback to the Prometheus text format in case of invalid/missing Content-Type and fail the scrape instead. Add ability to specify a `fallback_scrape_protocol` in the scrape config. #15136\\n199: * [CHANGE] Remote-write: default enable_http2 to false. #15219\\n200: * [CHANGE] Scraping: normalize \\\"le\\\" and \\\"quantile\\\" label values upon ingestion. #15164\\n201: * [CHANGE] Scraping: config `scrape_classic_histograms` was renamed to `always_scrape_classic_histograms`. #15178\\n202: * [CHANGE] Config: remove expand-external-labels flag, expand external labels env vars by default. #14657\\n203: * [CHANGE] Disallow configuring AM with the v1 api. #13883\\n204: * [CHANGE] regexp `.` now matches all characters (performance improvement). #14505\\n205: * [CHANGE] `holt_winters` is now called `double_exponential_smoothing` and moves behind the [experimental-promql-functions feature flag](https://prometheus.io/docs/prometheus/latest/feature_flags/#experimental-promql-functions). #14930\\n206: * [CHANGE] API: The OTLP receiver endpoint can now be enabled using `--web.enable-otlp-receiver` instead of `--enable-feature=otlp-write-receiver`. #14894\\n207: * [CHANGE] Prometheus will not add or remove port numbers from the target address. `no-default-scrape-port` feature flag removed. #14160\\n208: * [CHANGE] Logging: the format of log lines has changed a little, along with the adoption of Go's Structured Logging package. #14906\\n209: * [CHANGE] Don't create extra `_created` timeseries if feature-flag `created-timestamp-zero-ingestion` is enabled. #14738\\n210: * [CHANGE] Float literals and time durations being the same is now a stable fetaure. #15111\\n211: * [CHANGE] UI: The old web UI has been replaced by a completely new one that is less cluttered and adds a few new features (PromLens-style tree view, better metrics explorer, \\\"Explain\\\" tab). However, it is still missing some features of the old UI (notably, exemplar display and heatmaps). To switch back to the old UI, you can use the feature flag `--enable-feature=old-ui` for the time being. #14872\\n212: * [CHANGE] PromQL: Range selectors and the lookback delta are now left-open, i.e. a sample coinciding with the lower time limit is excluded rather than included. #13904\\n213: * [CHANGE] Kubernetes SD: Remove support for `discovery.k8s.io/v1beta1` API version of EndpointSlice. This version is no longer served as of Kubernetes v1.25. #14365\\n214: * [CHANGE] Kubernetes SD: Remove support for `networking.k8s.io/v1beta1` API version of Ingress. This version is no longer served as of Kubernetes v1.22. #14365\\n215: * [CHANGE] UTF-8: Enable UTF-8 support by default. Prometheus now allows all UTF-8 characters in metric and label names. The corresponding `utf8-name` feature flag has been removed. #14705, #15258\\n216: * [CHANGE] Console: Remove example files for the console feature. Users can continue using the console feature by supplying their own JavaScript and templates. #14807\\n217: * [CHANGE] SD: Enable the new service discovery manager by default. This SD manager does not restart unchanged discoveries upon reloading. This makes reloads faster and reduces pressure on service discoveries' sources. The corresponding `new-service-discovery-manager` feature flag has been removed. #14770\\n218: * [CHANGE] Agent mode has been promoted to stable. The feature flag `agent` has been removed. To run Prometheus in Agent mode, use the new `--agent` cmdline arg instead. #14747\\n219: * [CHANGE] Remove deprecated `remote-write-receiver`,`promql-at-modifier`, and `promql-negative-offset` endpoint. #15399\\n191: \\n192: ## 3.0.0 / 2024-11-14\\n193: \\n194: This release includes new features such as a brand new UI and UTF-8 support enabled by default. As this marks the first new major version in seven years, several breaking changes are introduced. The breaking changes are mainly around the removal of deprecated feature flags and CLI arguments, and the full list can be found below. For users that want to upgrade we recommend to read through our [migration guide](https://prometheus.io/docs/prometheus/3.0/migration/).\\n195: \\n196: * [CHANGE] Set the `GOMAXPROCS` variable automatically to match the Linux CPU quota. Use `--no-auto-gomaxprocs` to disable it. The `auto-gomaxprocs` feature flag was removed. #15376\\n197: * [CHANGE] Set the `GOMEMLIMIT` variable automatically to match the Linux container memory limit. Use `--no-auto-gomemlimit` to disable it. The `auto-gomemlimit` feature flag was removed. #15373\\n198: * [CHANGE] Scraping: Remove implicit fallback to the Prometheus text format in case of invalid/missing Content-Type and fail the scrape instead. Add ability to specify a `fallback_scrape_protocol` in the scrape config. #15136\\n199: * [CHANGE] Remote-write: default enable_http2 to false. #15219\\n200: * [CHANGE] Scraping: normalize \\\"le\\\" and \\\"quantile\\\" label values upon ingestion. #15164\\n201: * [CHANGE] Scraping: config `scrape_classic_histograms` was renamed to `always_scrape_classic_histograms`. #15178\\n202: * [CHANGE] Config: remove expand-external-labels flag, expand external labels env vars by default. #14657\\n203: * [CHANGE] Disallow configuring AM with the v1 api. #13883\\n204: * [CHANGE] regexp `.` now matches all characters (performance improvement). #14505\\n205: * [CHANGE] `holt_winters` is now called `double_exponential_smoothing` and moves behind the [experimental-promql-functions feature flag](https://prometheus.io/docs/prometheus/latest/feature_flags/#experimental-promql-functions). #14930\\n206: * [CHANGE] API: The OTLP receiver endpoint can now be enabled using `--web.enable-otlp-receiver` instead of `--enable-feature=otlp-write-receiver`. #14894\\n207: * [CHANGE] Prometheus will not add or remove port numbers from the target address. `no-default-scrape-port` feature flag removed. #14160\\n208: * [CHANGE] Logging: the format of log lines has changed a little, along with the adoption of Go's Structured Logging package. #14906\\n209: * [CHANGE] Don't create extra `_created` timeseries if feature-flag `created-timestamp-zero-ingestion` is enabled. #14738\\n210: * [CHANGE] Float literals and time durations being the same is now a stable fetaure. #15111\\n211: * [CHANGE] UI: The old web UI has been replaced by a completely new one that is less cluttered and adds a few new features (PromLens-style tree view, better metrics explorer, \\\"Explain\\\" tab). However, it is still missing some features of the old UI (notably, exemplar display and heatmaps). To switch back to the old UI, you can use the feature flag `--enable-feature=old-ui` for the time being. #14872\\n212: * [CHANGE] PromQL: Range selectors and the lookback delta are now left-open, i.e. a sample coinciding with the lower time limit is excluded rather than included. #13904\\n213: * [CHANGE] Kubernetes SD: Remove support for `discovery.k8s.io/v1beta1` API version of EndpointSlice. This version is no longer served as of Kubernetes v1.25. #14365\\n214: * [CHANGE] Kubernetes SD: Remove support for `networking.k8s.io/v1beta1` API version of Ingress. This version is no longer served as of Kubernetes v1.22. #14365\\n215: * [CHANGE] UTF-8: Enable UTF-8 support by default. Prometheus now allows all UTF-8 characters in metric and label names. The corresponding `utf8-name` feature flag has been removed. #14705, #15258\\n216: * [CHANGE] Console: Remove example files for the console feature. Users can continue using the console feature by supplying their own JavaScript and templates. #14807\\n217: * [CHANGE] SD: Enable the new service discovery manager by default. This SD manager does not restart unchanged discoveries upon reloading. This makes reloads faster and reduces pressure on service discoveries' sources. The corresponding `new-service-discovery-manager` feature flag has been removed. #14770\\n218: * [CHANGE] Agent mode has been promoted to stable. The feature flag `agent` has been removed. To run Prometheus in Agent mode, use the new `--agent` cmdline arg instead. #14747\\n219: * [CHANGE] Remove deprecated `remote-write-receiver`,`promql-at-modifier`, and `promql-negative-offset` ## 3.0.0 / 2024-11-14\n193: \n194: This release includes new features such as a brand new UI and UTF-8 support enabled by default. As this marks the first new major version in seven years, several breaking changes are introduced. The breaking changes are mainly around the removal of deprecated feature flags and CLI arguments, and the full list can be found below. For users that want to upgrade we recommend to read through our [migration guide](https://prometheus.io/docs/prometheus/3.0/migration/).\n195: \n196: * [CHANGE] Set the `GOMAXPROCS` variable automatically to match the Linux CPU quota. Use `--no-auto-gomaxprocs` to disable it. The `auto-gomaxprocs` feature flag was removed. #15376\n197: * [CHANGE] Set the `GOMEMLIMIT` variable automatically to match the Linux container memory limit. Use `--no-auto-gomemlimit` to disable it. The `auto-gomemlimit` feature flag was removed. #15373\n198: * [CHANGE] Scraping: Remove implicit fallback to the Prometheus text format in case of invalid/missing Content-Type and fail the scrape instead. Add ability to specify a `fallback_scrape_protocol` in the scrape config. #15136\n199: * [CHANGE] Remote-write: default enable_http2 to false. #15219\n200: * [CHANGE] Scraping: normalize \"le\" and \"quantile\" label values upon ingestion. #15164\n201: * [CHANGE] Scraping: config `scrape_classic_histograms` was renamed to `always_scrape_classic_histograms`. #15178\n202: * [CHANGE] Config: remove expand-external-labels flag, expand external labels env vars by default. #14657\n203: * [CHANGE] Disallow configuring AM with the v1 api. #13883\n204: * [CHANGE] regexp `.` now matches all characters (performance improvement). #14505\n205: * [CHANGE] `holt_winters` is now called `double_exponential_smoothing` and moves behind the [experimental-promql-functions feature flag](https://prometheus.io/docs/prometheus/latest/feature_flags/#experimental-promql-functions). #14930\n206: * [CHANGE] API: The OTLP receiver endpoint can now be enabled using `--web.enable-otlp-receiver` instead of `--enable-feature=otlp-write-receiver`. #14894\n207: * [CHANGE] Prometheus will not add or remove port numbers from the target address. `no-default-scrape-port` feature flag removed. #14160\n208: * [CHANGE] Logging: the format of log lines has changed a little, along with the adoption of Go's Structured Logging package. #14906\n209: * [CHANGE] Don't create extra `_created` timeseries if feature-flag `created-timestamp-zero-ingestion` is enabled. #14738\n210: * [CHANGE] Float literals and time durations being the same is now a stable fetaure. #15111\n211: * [CHANGE] UI: The old web UI has been replaced by a completely new one that is less cluttered and adds a few new features (PromLens-style tree view, better metrics explorer, \"Explain\" tab). However, it is still missing some features of the old UI (notably, exemplar display and heatmaps). To switch back to the old UI, you can use the feature flag `--enable-feature=old-ui` for the time being. #14872\n212: * [CHANGE] PromQL: Range selectors and the lookback delta are now left-open, i.e. a sample coinciding with the lower time limit is excluded rather than included. #13904\n213: * [CHANGE] Kubernetes SD: Remove support for `discovery.k8s.io/v1beta1` API version of EndpointSlice. This version is no longer served as of Kubernetes v1.25. #14365\n214: * [CHANGE] Kubernetes SD: Remove support for `networking.k8s.io/v1beta1` API version of Ingress. This version is no longer served as of Kubernetes v1.22. #14365\n215: * [CHANGE] UTF-8: Enable UTF-8 support by default. Prometheus now allows all UTF-8 characters in metric and label names. The corresponding `utf8-name` feature flag has been removed. #14705, #15258\n216: * [CHANGE] Console: Remove example files for the console feature. Users can continue using the console feature by supplying their own JavaScript and templates. #14807\n217: * [CHANGE] SD: Enable the new service discovery manager by default. This SD manager does not restart unchanged discoveries upon reloading. This makes reloads faster and reduces pressure on service discoveries' sources. The corresponding `new-service-discovery-manager` feature flag has been removed. #14770\n218: * [CHANGE] Agent mode has been promoted to stable. The feature flag `agent` has been removed. To run Prometheus in Agent mode, use the new `--agent` cmdline arg instead. #14747\n219: * [CHANGE] Remove deprecated `remote-write-receiver`,`promql-at-modifier`, and `promql-negative-offset` feature flags. #13456, #14526\n220: * [CHANGE] Remove deprecated `storage.tsdb.allow-overlapping-blocks`, `alertmanager.timeout`, and `storage.tsdb.retention` flags. #14640, #14643\n221: * [FEATURE] OTLP receiver: Ability to skip UTF-8 normalization using `otlp.translation_strategy = NoUTF8EscapingWithSuffixes` configuration option. #15384\n222: * [FEATURE] Support config reload automatically - feature flag `auto-reload-config`. #14769, #15011\n223: * [ENHANCEMENT] Scraping, rules: handle targets reappearing, or rules moving group, when out-of-order is enabled. #14710\n224: * [ENHANCEMENT] Tools: add debug printouts to promtool rules unit testing #15196\n225: * [ENHANCEMENT] Scraping: support Created-Timestamp feature on native histograms. #14694\n226: * [ENHANCEMENT] UI: Many fixes and improvements. #14898, #14899, #14907, #14908, #14912, #14913, #14914, #14931, #14940, #14945, #14946, #14972, #14981, #14982, #14994, #15096\n227: * [ENHANCEMENT] UI: Web UI now displays notifications, e.g. when starting up and shutting down. #15082\n228: * [ENHANCEMENT] PromQL: Introduce exponential interpolation for native histograms. #14677\n229: * [ENHANCEMENT] TSDB: Add support for ingestion of out-of-order native histogram samples. #14850, #14546\n230: * [ENHANCEMENT] Alerts: remove metrics for removed Alertmanagers. #13909\n231: * [ENHANCEMENT] Kubernetes SD: Support postings by doubling. #14721\n237: * [PERF] Relabeling: Optimize adding a constant label pair. #12180\n238: * [BUGFIX] Scraping: Don't log errors on empty scrapes. #15357\n239: * [BUGFIX] UI: fix This creates a race where:\n\n1. Samples are stuck in old shard queues that are being flushed\n2. The metric gets reset to 0\n\n\n3. New samples are added to new shards, increasing the metric\n4. But old samples may be lost or stalled if the flushDeadline is exceeded\n\nThe core issue is that resetting `pendingSamples` to 0 while old shards are still flushing creates a window where sample counts become inaccurate. When resharding occurs:\n   - updateShardsLoop() calculates desired shards\n   - It sends the new shard count on reshardChan\n   - reshardLoop() receives this and calls stop() then start()\n\n2. The bug is in start() at line 1241:\n   - `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)` - resets the metric\n   - But the old shards are still being flushed!\n   - Any samples left in the old queue that don't flush within flushDeadline are dropped\n   - But the metric is reset to 0, so they're \"forgotten\"\n\n3. The race condition:\n   - Old shards have enqueued samples incrementing pendingSamples\n   - stop() closes softShutdown and starts flushing (line 1275-1284)\n   - But if flush takes > flushDeadline, hardShutdown() is called (line 1293)\n   - Samples are dropped (line 1566-1577 in runShard)\n   - Then start() is called, resetting pendingSamples to 0\n   - So the metric doesn't reflect the dropped samples\n\nActually, looking more carefully at the sequence in reshardLoop (line 1189-1194):\n```go\ncase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n    // We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n    // flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n    // order.\n    t.shards.stop()\n    t.shards.start(numShards)\n```\n\nThe comment says \"after we have stopped (and therefore completely flushed) the oldShards\". But the stop() function doesn't guarantee complete flushing - it waits up to flushDeadline, then does a hard shutdown if needed!\n\n\nThe core issue is that start() resets the pending samples counter to zero while old shards may still be dropping data during their hard shutdown phase. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01T91bv8DTKHDbrckSSb6vzP","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01AMEcvq88T5Ko48sqvibsjX","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Prometheus remote-write queue system experiences intermittent sample loss and stalled shards during dynamic resharding operations. When target discovery changes trigger shard count adjustments, a race condition between metric resetting and incomplete queue flushing causes samples to be silently dropped while metrics incorrectly report zero pending samples.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n### Primary Issue: Metric Reset During Incomplete Flush\n\n**File**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, **Function**: `shards.start()` (line 1237-1266)\n\nThe bug occurs at line 1241:\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) start(n int) {\n    s.mtx.Lock()\n    defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n\n    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // Line 1241 - RESETS METRIC\n    s.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n```\n\nWhen resharding is triggered in `reshardLoop()` (line 1184-1199):\n```go\ncase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n    t.shards.stop()      // Line 1193 - Stops old shards\n    t.shards.start(numShards)  // Line 1194 - Starts new shards\n```\n\nThe sequence creates a race condition:\n\n1. **stop() is called** (line 1269-1305):\n   - Closes `softShutdown` channel (line 1275)\n   - All queues attempt FlushAndShutdown (line 1284)\n   - Waits up to `flushDeadline` for completion (line 1289)\n\n2. **If flush times out** (line 1289):\n   - Hard shutdown is triggered (line 1293)\n   - Old shard goroutines begin dropping samples (line 1566-1577 in `runShard`)\n   - Samples in queues are lost\n\n3. **start() is called while old shards still dropping**:\n   - **Immediately resets metric: `pendingSamples.Set(0)`** (line 1241)\n   - Creates new queue array (line 1244-1246)\n   - Starts new shard goroutines (line 1263-1265)\n   - Dropped samples from old shards are never reflected in metrics\n\n### Secondary Issue: Shard Assignment Changes During Transition\n\n**File**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, **Function**: `enqueue()` (line 1312-1341)\n\nThe shard assignment is computed by: `shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))` (line 1315)\n\nDuring resharding:\n- Old queues have count `N`\n- New queues have count `M` (where N ≠ M due to scaling)\n- Samples that fail to enqueue during shutdown retry later\n- They now hash to potentially different shard indices\n- This can create unbalanced load or ordering issues\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key Code Paths\n\n**Resharding Trigger** (`queue_manager.go:1057-1082`):\n```go\nfunc (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n    ...\n    case t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n        t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n        t.numShards = desiredShards\n```\n\n**Sample Enqueueing** (`queue_manager.go:1312-1341`):\n- Line 1326: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()` - increments when added\n- Line 1241: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)` - **unconditionally reset!**\n- No corresponding decrement when old samples are dropped\n\n**Sample Drop Path** (`queue_manager.go:1561-1578`):\n```go\ncase <-ctx.Done():\n    droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))  // Only if hard shutdown\n    s.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n```\n\nThe problem: When `Set(0)` is called in `start()`, this overrides any attempted decrements from old shards.\n\n### Timing Window\n\nThe issue manifests as **intermittent** because it depends on:\n1. **Resharding trigger**: Target discovery changes (add/remove targets)\n2. **Load at trigger time**: Number of samples in flight when resharding begins\n3. **Flush deadline**: Whether old queues can send all samples within timeout\n4. **Remote backend latency**: If remote storage is slow, flush times out\n\nScenarios that increase probability:\n- High sample volume during discovery change\n- Slow remote-write backend (causing sends to take > flushDeadline)\n- Frequent target discovery updates\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Primary Package\n- **`storage/remote/`**: Queue management, resharding logic\n\n### Specific Files\n- `queue_manager.go`: Core resharding mechanism (lines 1057-1305)\n- Lines 1237-1266: `shards.start()` - the bug trigger\n- Lines 1184-1199: `reshardLoop()` - orchestrates resharding\n- Lines 1269-1305: `shards.stop()` - initiates flush/shutdown\n- Lines 1312-1341: `enqueue()` - shard assignment\n\n### Metrics Affected\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - reports 0 despite queued samples\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` - transitions occur during vulnerable window\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - incomplete on timeout\n\n## Mechanism: Why Shards Stall\n\n1. **During resharding transition window**:\n   - `softShutdown` is closed in old shards (line 1275)\n   - `enqueue()` fails for new samples (line 1317-1318)\n   - No new shards exist yet (sequential: stop → start)\n\n2. **Failed samples in WAL retry loop** (line 815-866 example):\n   ```go\n   for {\n       if t.shards.enqueue(...) {\n           continue outer\n       }\n       t.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n       time.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n       // Retry with exponential backoff\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **When start() completes**:\n   - Retrying samples go to new queues\n   - But if new shard count differs, hash assignments change\n   - Some historical samples may hash to different (potentially saturated) shards\n\n4. **Result**:\n   - Specific shards appear stuck with `samples_pending > 0`\n   - Other shards drain normally\n   - Uneven load distribution persists\n\n## Diagnostic Evidence\n\n### Logs to Watch For\n- `\"Remote storage resharding\"` - indicates resharding started\n- `\"Currently resharding, skipping\"` - resharding in progress (from line 1076)\n- `\"Failed to flush all samples on shutdown\"` - samples dropped (from line 1299)\n- `\"enqueue_retries_total\"` increasing - samples failing to enqueue (metric)\n\n### Metrics to Correlate\n1. `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` - changes during resharding\n2. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - should **not** drop to 0 during transition\n3. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - increase during timeout\n4. `prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total` - spikes during resharding window\n5. Check if samples appear in queued-but-dropped metrics\n   - Correlate timestamp of resharding with metric spikes\n\n4. **Check remote backend latency**:\n   - If backend slowness triggered timeout, check remote latency metrics\n   - Confirm `flushDeadline` is insufficient for current backend\n\n## Related Issues\n\n- CHANGELOG #13562: \"Disable resharding during active retry backoffs\"\n- CHANGELOG #7122: \"Fixed blocked resharding edge case\"\n- These suggest this is a known challenging area with prior bugs\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe intermittent sample loss during resharding is caused by unconditionally resetting the `pendingSamples` metric while old queue shards are still in the process of flushing (and potentially timing out and hard-shutting down). The metric reset hides dropped samples, and the shard reassignment during the vulnerable window creates asymmetric load on new shards, causing some to appear stalled. When target discovery changes trigger shard count adjustments, a race condition between metric resetting and incomplete queue flushing causes samples to be silently dropped while metrics incorrectly report zero pending samples.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n### Primary Issue: Metric Reset During Incomplete Flush\n\n**File**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, **Function**: `shards.start()` (line 1237-1266)\n\nThe bug occurs at line 1241:\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) start(n int) {\n    s.mtx.Lock()\n    defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n\n    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // Line 1241 - RESETS METRIC\n    s.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n```\n\nWhen resharding is triggered in `reshardLoop()` (line 1184-1199):\n```go\ncase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n    t.shards.stop()      // Line 1193 - Stops old shards\n    t.shards.start(numShards)  // Line 1194 - Starts new shards\n```\n\nThe sequence creates a race condition:\n\n1. **stop() is called** (line 1269-1305):\n   - Closes `softShutdown` channel (line 1275)\n   - All queues attempt FlushAndShutdown (line 1284)\n   - Waits up to `flushDeadline` for completion (line 1289)\n\n2. **If flush times out** (line 1289):\n   - Hard shutdown is triggered (line 1293)\n   - Old shard goroutines begin dropping samples (line 1566-1577 in `runShard`)\n   - Samples in queues are lost\n\n3. **start() is called while old shards still dropping**:\n   - **Immediately resets metric: `pendingSamples.Set(0)`** (line 1241)\n   - Creates new queue array (line 1244-1246)\n   - Starts new shard goroutines (line 1263-1265)\n   - Dropped samples from old shards are never reflected in metrics\n\n### Secondary Issue: Shard Assignment Changes During Transition\n\n**File**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, **Function**: `enqueue()` (line 1312-1341)\n\nThe shard assignment is computed by: `shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))` (line 1315)\n\nDuring resharding:\n- Old queues have count `N`\n- New queues have count `M` (where N ≠ M due to scaling)\n- Samples that fail to enqueue during shutdown retry later\n- They now hash to potentially different shard indices\n- This can create unbalanced load or ordering issues\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key Code Paths\n\n**Resharding Trigger** (`queue_manager.go:1057-1082`):\n```go\nfunc (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n    ...\n    case t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n        t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n        t.numShards = desiredShards\n```\n\n**Sample Enqueueing** (`queue_manager.go:1312-1341`):\n- Line 1326: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()` - increments when added\n- Line 1241: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)` - **unconditionally reset!**\n- No corresponding decrement when old samples are dropped\n\n**Sample Drop Path** (`queue_manager.go:1561-1578`):\n```go\ncase <-ctx.Done():\n    droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))  // Only if hard shutdown\n    s.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n```\n\nThe problem: When `Set(0)` is called in `start()`, this overrides any attempted decrements from old shards.\n\n### Timing Window\n\nThe issue manifests as **intermittent** because it depends on:\n1. **Resharding trigger**: Target discovery changes (add/remove targets)\n2. **Load at trigger time**: Number of samples in flight when resharding begins\n3. **Flush deadline**: Whether old queues can send all samples within timeout\n4. **Remote backend latency**: If remote storage is slow, flush times out\n\nScenarios that increase probability:\n- High sample volume during discovery change\n- Slow remote-write backend (causing sends to take > flushDeadline)\n- Frequent target discovery updates\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Primary Package\n- **`storage/remote/`**: Queue management, resharding logic\n\n### Specific Files\n- `queue_manager.go`: Core resharding mechanism (lines 1057-1305)\n- Lines 1237-1266: `shards.start()` - the bug trigger\n- Lines 1184-1199: `reshardLoop()` - orchestrates resharding\n- Lines 1269-1305: `shards.stop()` - initiates flush/shutdown\n- Lines 1312-1341: `enqueue()` - shard assignment\n\n### Metrics Affected\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - reports 0 despite queued samples\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` - transitions occur during vulnerable window\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - incomplete on timeout\n\n## Mechanism: Why Shards Stall\n\n1. **During resharding transition window**:\n   - `softShutdown` is closed in old shards (line 1275)\n   - `enqueue()` fails for new samples (line 1317-1318)\n   - No new shards exist yet (sequential: stop → start)\n\n2. **Failed samples in WAL retry loop** (line 815-866 example):\n   ```go\n   for {\n       if t.shards.enqueue(...) {\n           continue outer\n       }\n       t.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n       time.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n       // Retry with exponential backoff\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **When start() completes**:\n   - Retrying samples go to new queues\n   - But if new shard count differs, hash assignments change\n   - Some historical samples may hash to different (potentially saturated) shards\n\n4. **Result**:\n   - Specific shards appear stuck with `samples_pending > 0`\n   - Other shards drain normally\n   - Uneven load distribution persists\n\n## Diagnostic Evidence\n\n### Logs to Watch For\n- `\"Remote storage resharding\"` - indicates resharding started\n- `\"Currently resharding, skipping\"` - resharding in progress (from line 1076)\n- `\"Failed to flush all samples on shutdown\"` - samples dropped (from line 1299)\n- `\"enqueue_retries_total\"` increasing - samples failing to enqueue (metric)\n\n### Metrics to Correlate\n1. `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` - changes during resharding\n2. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - should **not** drop to 0 during transition\n3. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - increase during timeout\n4. `prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total` - spikes during resharding window\n5. Query: Which shards have high pending values?\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending{shard=\"X\"}` if exposed per-shard\n\n### Reproduction Conditions\n- Trigger target discovery changes while sending high sample volume\n- Configure remote backend with high latency\n- Set low `flushDeadline` in config\n- Monitor metrics during target add/remove operations\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\n**Option 1: Atomic Metric Update (Recommended)**\n- Track pending samples from old shards before reset\n- Only reset new shards' metrics\n- Don't call `Set(0)` unconditionally\n\n**Option 2: Prevent Resharding During Flush**\n- Don't trigger new resharding until old shards fully shutdown\n- Wait for `s.done` channel before calling `start()`\n- Currently already done sequentially, so issue is timing\n\n**Option 3: Increase Flush Timeout**\n- Current default `flushDeadline` may be too aggressive\n- Extend to allow slow backends to drain queues\n- Less ideal: masks the real issue\n\n### Diagnostic Steps for Root Cause Confirmation\n\n1. **Query metrics during target discovery change**:\n   ```\n   # Watch when resharding starts\n   prometheus_remote_storage_shards\n\n   # Should NOT drop to 0 mid-resharding\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending\n\n   # Count dropped samples\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total\n   ```\n\n2. **Enable debug logging** in remote storage:\n   - When target discovery changes trigger shard count adjustments, a race condition between metric resetting and incomplete queue flushing causes samples to be silently dropped while metrics incorrectly report zero pending samples.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n### Primary Issue: Metric Reset During Incomplete Flush\n\n**File**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, **Function**: `shards.start()` (line 1237-1266)\n\nThe bug occurs at line 1241:\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) start(n int) {\n    s.mtx.Lock()\n    defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n\n    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // Line 1241 - RESETS METRIC\n    s.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n```\n\nWhen resharding is triggered in `reshardLoop()` (line 1184-1199):\n```go\ncase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n    t.shards.stop()      // Line 1193 - Stops old shards\n    t.shards.start(numShards)  // Line 1194 - Starts new shards\n```\n\nThe sequence creates a race condition:\n\n1. **stop() is called** (line 1269-1305):\n   - Closes `softShutdown` channel (line 1275)\n   - All queues attempt FlushAndShutdown (line 1284)\n   - Waits up to `flushDeadline` for completion (line 1289)\n\n2. **If flush times out** (line 1289):\n   - Hard shutdown is triggered (line 1293)\n   - Old shard goroutines begin dropping samples (line 1566-1577 in `runShard`)\n   - Samples in queues are lost\n\n3. **start() is called while old shards still dropping**:\n   - **Immediately resets metric: `pendingSamples.Set(0)`** (line 1241)\n   - Creates new queue array (line 1244-1246)\n   - Starts new shard goroutines (line 1263-1265)\n   - Dropped samples from old shards are never reflected in metrics\n\n### Secondary Issue: Shard Assignment Changes During Transition\n\n**File**: `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, **Function**: `enqueue()` (line 1312-1341)\n\nThe shard assignment is computed by: `shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))` (line 1315)\n\nDuring resharding:\n- Old queues have count `N`\n- New queues have count `M` (where N ≠ M due to scaling)\n- Samples that fail to enqueue during shutdown retry later\n- They now hash to potentially different shard indices\n- This can create unbalanced load or ordering issues\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key Code Paths\n\n**Resharding Trigger** (`queue_manager.go:1057-1082`):\n```go\nfunc (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {\n    ...\n    case t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n        t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n        t.numShards = desiredShards\n```\n\n**Sample Enqueueing** (`queue_manager.go:1312-1341`):\n- Line 1326: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()` - increments when added\n- Line 1241: `s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)` - **unconditionally reset!**\n- No corresponding decrement when old samples are dropped\n\n**Sample Drop Path** (`queue_manager.go:1561-1578`):\n```go\ncase <-ctx.Done():\n    droppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n    s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))  // Only if hard shutdown\n    s.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n```\n\nThe problem: When `Set(0)` is called in `start()`, this overrides any attempted decrements from old shards.\n\n### Timing Window\n\nThe issue manifests as **intermittent** because it depends on:\n1. **Resharding trigger**: Target discovery changes (add/remove targets)\n2. **Load at trigger time**: Number of samples in flight when resharding begins\n3. **Flush deadline**: Whether old queues can send all samples within timeout\n4. **Remote backend latency**: If remote storage is slow, flush times out\n\nScenarios that increase probability:\n- High sample volume during discovery change\n- Slow remote-write backend (causing sends to take > flushDeadline)\n- Frequent target discovery updates\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Primary Package\n- **`storage/remote/`**: Queue management, resharding logic\n\n### Specific Files\n- `queue_manager.go`: Core resharding mechanism (lines 1057-1305)\n- Lines 1237-1266: `shards.start()` - the bug trigger\n- Lines 1184-1199: `reshardLoop()` - orchestrates resharding\n- Lines 1269-1305: `shards.stop()` - initiates flush/shutdown\n- Lines 1312-1341: `enqueue()` - shard assignment\n\n### Metrics Affected\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - reports 0 despite queued samples\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` - transitions occur during vulnerable window\n- `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - incomplete on timeout\n\n## Mechanism: Why Shards Stall\n\n1. **During resharding transition window**:\n   - `softShutdown` is closed in old shards (line 1275)\n   - `enqueue()` fails for new samples (line 1317-1318)\n   - No new shards exist yet (sequential: stop → start)\n\n2. **Failed samples in WAL retry loop** (line 815-866 example):\n   ```go\n   for {\n       if t.shards.enqueue(...) {\n           continue outer\n       }\n       t.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n       time.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n       // Retry with exponential backoff\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **When start() completes**:\n   - Retrying samples go to new queues\n   - But if new shard count differs, hash assignments change\n   - Some historical samples may hash to different (potentially saturated) shards\n\n4. **Result**:\n   - Specific shards appear stuck with `samples_pending > 0`\n   - Other shards drain normally\n   - Uneven load distribution persists\n\n## Diagnostic Evidence\n\n### Logs to Watch For\n- `\"Remote storage resharding\"` - indicates resharding started\n- `\"Currently resharding, skipping\"` - resharding in progress (from line 1076)\n- `\"Failed to flush all samples on shutdown\"` - samples dropped (from line 1299)\n- `\"enqueue_retries_total\"` increasing - samples failing to enqueue (metric)\n\n### Metrics to Correlate\n1. `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` - changes during resharding\n2. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - should **not** drop to 0 during transition\n3. `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - increase during timeout\n4. `prometheus_remote_storage_enqueue_retries_total` - spikes during resharding window\n5. Query: Which shards have high pending values?\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending{shard=\"X\"}` if exposed per-shard\n\n### Reproduction Conditions\n- Trigger target discovery changes while sending high sample volume\n- Configure remote backend with high latency\n- Set low `flushDeadline` in config\n- Monitor metrics during target add/remove operations\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\n**Option 1: Atomic Metric Update (Recommended)**\n- Track pending samples from old shards before reset\n- Only reset new shards' metrics\n- Don't call `Set(0)` unconditionally\n\n**Option 2: Prevent Resharding During Flush**\n- Don't trigger new resharding until old shards fully shutdown\n- Wait for `s.done` channel before calling `start()`\n- Currently already done sequentially, so issue is timing\n\n**Option 3: Increase Flush Timeout**\n- Current default `flushDeadline` may be too aggressive\n- Extend to allow slow backends to drain queues\n- Less ideal: masks the real issue\n\n### Diagnostic Steps for Root Cause Confirmation\n\n1. **Query metrics during target discovery change**:\n   ```\n   # Watch when resharding starts\n   prometheus_remote_storage_shards\n\n   # Should NOT drop to 0 mid-resharding\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending\n\n   # Count dropped samples\n   prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total\n   ```\n\n2. **Enable debug logging** in remote storage:\n   - Check logs for \"Resharding done\" log message\n   - Verify samples_pending > 0 at that point\n   - If pending drops to 0 immediately after, bug confirmed\n\n3. **Trace queue depth**:\n   - Check old shard queue lengths before stop()\n   - Check if samples appear in queued-but-dropped metrics\n   - Correlate timestamp of resharding with metric spikes\n\n4. **Check remote backend latency**:\n   - If backend slowness triggered timeout, check remote latency metrics\n   - Confirm `flushDeadline` is insufficient for current backend\n\n## Related Issues\n\n- CHANGELOG #13562: \"Disable resharding during active retry backoffs\"\n- CHANGELOG #7122: \"Fixed blocked resharding edge case\"\n- These suggest this is a known challenging area with prior bugs\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe intermittent sample loss during resharding is caused by unconditionally resetting the `pendingSamples` metric while old queue shards are still in the process of flushing (and potentially timing out and hard-shutting down). The metric reset hides dropped samples, and the shard reassignment during the vulnerable window creates asymmetric load on new shards, causing some to appear stalled. The issue is intermittent because it depends on the timing of target discovery changes relative to ongoing sample processing and remote backend latency.\n","numLines":226,"startLine":1,"totalLines":226}}}
